The conflict had forced 40,000 to 50,000 civilians to flee their homes and seek shelter on the Chinese side of the border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> During the incident, the government of China was accused of giving military assistance to the <a href="/wiki/Kokang_Chinese" title="Kokang Chinese">ethnic Chinese</a> rebels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> Clashes between Burmese troops and local insurgent groups have continued, fuelling tensions between China and Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Period_of_liberalisation.2C_2011.E2.80.932021"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Period_of_liberalisation,_2011â2021">Period of liberalisation, 2011â2021</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%932015_Myanmar_political_reforms" title="2011â2015 Myanmar political reforms">2011â2015 Myanmar political reforms</a></div>
<p>The military-backed Government had promulgated a <a href="/wiki/Roadmap_to_democracy" title="Roadmap to democracy">"Roadmap to Discipline-flourishing Democracy"</a> in 1993, but the process appeared to stall several times, until 2008 when the Government published a new draft national constitution, and organised a (flawed) national referendum which adopted it. The new constitution provided for election of a national assembly with powers to appoint a president, while practically ensuring army control at all levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2731" data-file-width="4096" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Hillary_Clinton_at_home_of_Aung_San_Suu_Kyi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> with <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> and her staff at her home in Yangon, 2012</div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/2010_Myanmar_general_election" title="2010 Myanmar general election">general election in 2010</a> - the first for twenty years - was boycotted by the <a href="/wiki/National_League_for_Democracy" title="National League for Democracy">NLD</a>. The military-backed <a href="/wiki/Union_Solidarity_and_Development_Party" title="Union Solidarity and Development Party">Union Solidarity and Development Party</a> declared victory, stating that it had been favoured by 80 per cent of the votes; fraud, however, was alleged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tni.org_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-tni.org-114">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> A nominally civilian government was then formed, with retired general <a href="/wiki/Thein_Sein" title="Thein Sein">Thein Sein</a> as President.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>A series of liberalising political and economic actions â or reforms â then took place. By the end of 2011 these included the release of pro-democracy leader Aung San Suu Kyi from house arrest, the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_National_Human_Rights_Commission" title="Myanmar National Human Rights Commission">National Human Rights Commission</a>, the granting of general amnesties for more than 200 political prisoners, new labour laws that permitted labour unions and strikes, a relaxation of press censorship, and the regulation of currency practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> In response, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> visited Myanmar in December 2011 â the first visit by a US Secretary of State in more than fifty years<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> â meeting both President Thein Sein and opposition leader Aung San Suu Kyi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinton_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clinton-119">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_League_for_Democracy" title="National League for Democracy">NLD</a> party participated in the 2012 by-elections, facilitated by the government's abolition of the laws that previously barred it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> In the April 2012 <a href="/wiki/2012_Myanmar_by-elections" title="2012 Myanmar by-elections">by-elections</a>, the NLD won 43 of the 45 available seats. The 2012 by-elections were also the first time that international representatives were allowed to monitor the voting process in Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>Myanmar's improved international reputation was indicated by <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>'s approval of Myanmar's bid for the position of <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> chair in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Burma_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2938" data-file-width="1324" decoding="async" height="399" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Burma_en.png/180px-Burma_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Burma_en.png/270px-Burma_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Burma_en.png/360px-Burma_en.png 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Burma_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Myanmar and its divisions, including <a href="/wiki/Shan_State" title="Shan State">Shan State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kachin_State" title="Kachin State">Kachin State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rakhine_State" title="Rakhine State">Rakhine State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kayah_State" title="Kayah State">Karen State</a>.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_general_elections">2015 general elections</span></h4>
<p>General elections <a href="/wiki/2015_Myanmar_general_election" title="2015 Myanmar general election">were held on 8 November 2015</a>. These were the first openly contested elections held in Myanmar since the 1990 general election (which was annulled<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landmark_elections_2015_12_03_bbc_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-landmark_elections_2015_12_03_bbc-123">[121]</a></sup>). The results gave the NLD an <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">absolute majority</a> of seats in both chambers of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">national parliament</a>, enough to ensure that its candidate would become president, while NLD leader <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> is constitutionally barred from the presidency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landmark_elections_2015_12_03_bbc_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-landmark_elections_2015_12_03_bbc-123">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-national_league_wins_2015_11_13_bbc_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-national_league_wins_2015_11_13_bbc-124">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>The new parliament convened on 1 February 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> and on 15 March 2016, <a href="/wiki/Htin_Kyaw" title="Htin Kyaw">Htin Kyaw</a> was elected as the first non-military president since the military coup of 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> On 6 April 2016, <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> assumed the newly created role of <a href="/wiki/State_Counsellor_of_Myanmar" title="State Counsellor of Myanmar">state counsellor</a>, a role akin to a <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Myanmar" title="Prime Minister of Myanmar">prime minister</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_liberalisation_period">Analysis of liberalisation period</span></h4>
<p>Throughout this decade of apparent liberalisation, opinions differed whether a transition to <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democracy</a> was underway. To some it appeared merely that the Burmese military was allowing certain civil liberties while clandestinely institutionalising itself further into <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Myanmar" title="Politics of Myanmar">Burmese politics</a> and economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2020_elections_and_2021_military_coup_d.27.C3.A9tat"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020_elections_and_2021_military_coup_d'Ã©tat">2020 elections and 2021 military coup d'Ã©tat</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2021_Myanmar_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2021 Myanmar coup d'Ã©tat">2021 Myanmar coup d'Ã©tat</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_and_aftermath">Election and aftermath</span></h4>
<p>In Myanmar's 2020 parliamentary election,
the ostensibly ruling <a href="/wiki/National_League_for_Democracy" title="National League for Democracy">National League for Democracy (NLD)</a>, the party of State Counsellor <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>, competed with various other smaller parties â particularly the military-affiliated <a href="/wiki/Union_Solidarity_and_Development_Party" title="Union Solidarity and Development Party">Union Solidarity and Development Party (USDP)</a>. Other parties and individuals allied with specific ethnic minorities also ran for office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_election_2020_11_11_nytimes_com_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_election_2020_11_11_nytimes_com-131">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>Suu Kyi's NLD won the <a href="/wiki/2020_Myanmar_general_election" title="2020 Myanmar general election">2020 Myanmar general election</a> on 8 November in a landslide, again winning supermajorities in both houses<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_election_2020_11_11_nytimes_com_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_election_2020_11_11_nytimes_com-131">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suu_kyis_party_wins_2020_11_13_bbc_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-suu_kyis_party_wins_2020_11_13_bbc-132">[130]</a></sup>âwinning 396 out of 476 elected seats in parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commission_rejects_2021_01_29_apnews_com_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-commission_rejects_2021_01_29_apnews_com-133">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>The USDP, regarded as a proxy for the military, suffered a "humiliating" defeat<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters-134">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-defeated_2020_11_12_irrawaddy_com_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-defeated_2020_11_12_irrawaddy_com-135">[133]</a></sup>  â even worse than in 2015<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-defeated_2020_11_12_irrawaddy_com_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-defeated_2020_11_12_irrawaddy_com-135">[133]</a></sup> â capturing only 33 of the 476 elected seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commission_rejects_2021_01_29_apnews_com_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-commission_rejects_2021_01_29_apnews_com-133">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters-134">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>As the election results began emerging, the USDP rejected them, urging a new election with the military as observers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_election_2020_11_11_nytimes_com_131-2"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_election_2020_11_11_nytimes_com-131">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-defeated_2020_11_12_irrawaddy_com_135-2"><a href="#cite_note-defeated_2020_11_12_irrawaddy_com-135">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>More than 90 other smaller parties contested the vote, including more than 15 who complained of irregularities. However,  election observers declared there were no major irregularities in the voting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters_134-2"><a href="#cite_note-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters-134">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>The military â arguing that it had found over 8 million irregularities in voter lists, in over 300 townships â called on Myanmar's <a href="/wiki/Union_Election_Commission" title="Union Election Commission">Union Election Commission (UEC)</a> and government to review the results, but the commission dismissed the claims for lack of any evidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commission_rejects_2021_01_29_apnews_com_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-commission_rejects_2021_01_29_apnews_com-133">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_election_body_2021_01_28_irrawaddy_com_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_election_body_2021_01_28_irrawaddy_com-136">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>The election commission declared that any irregularities were too few and too minor to affect the outcome of the election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters_134-3"><a href="#cite_note-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters-134">[132]</a></sup> However, despite the election commission validating the NLD's overwhelming victory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_election_body_2021_01_28_irrawaddy_com_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_election_body_2021_01_28_irrawaddy_com-136">[134]</a></sup>  the USDP and Myanmar's military persistently alleged fraud<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-military_condemns_2021_01_15_irrawaddy_com_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-military_condemns_2021_01_15_irrawaddy_com-137">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-military_demands_2021_01_21_irrawaddy_com_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-military_demands_2021_01_21_irrawaddy_com-138">[136]</a></sup> and the military threatened to "take action".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters_134-4"><a href="#cite_note-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters-134">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Myanmar_military_2021_01_26_irrawaddy_com_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Myanmar_military_2021_01_26_irrawaddy_com-139">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-military_threats_channelnewsasia_com_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-military_threats_channelnewsasia_com-140">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-military_chief_warns_2021_01_28_irrawaddy_com_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-military_chief_warns_2021_01_28_irrawaddy_com-141">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coup_talk_2021_01_28_bangkokpost_com_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-coup_talk_2021_01_28_bangkokpost_com-142">[140]</a></sup>
In January, 2021, just before the new parliament was to be sworn in, The NLD announced that Suu Kyi would retain her State Counsellor role in the upcoming government.
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suu_kyi_to_keep_2021_01_25_irrawaddy_com_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-suu_kyi_to_keep_2021_01_25_irrawaddy_com-143">[141]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coup">Coup</span></h4>
<p>In the early morning of 1 February 2021, the day parliament was set to convene, the <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Tatmadaw</a>, Myanmar's military, detained State Counsellor <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> and other members of the ruling party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters_134-5"><a href="#cite_note-crisis_in_myanmar_2021_01_31_reuters-134">[132]</a></sup>
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021-02-01_bbc_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021-02-01_bbc-144">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup> The military handed power to military chief <a href="/wiki/Min_Aung_Hlaing" title="Min Aung Hlaing">Min Aung Hlaing</a> and declared a state of emergency for one year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suu_kyi_detained_2021_01_31_bloomberg_com_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-suu_kyi_detained_2021_01_31_bloomberg_com-146">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021-02-01_bbc_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021-02-01_bbc-144">[142]</a></sup> and began closing the borders, restricting travel and electronic communications nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>The military announced it would replace the existing election commission with a new one, and a military media outlet indicated new elections would be held in about one year â though the military avoided making an official commitment to that.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-2"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>State Counselor Aung San Suu Kyi and President Win Myint were placed under house arrest, and the military began filing various charges against them. The military expelled NLD party Members of Parliament from the capital city, <a href="/wiki/Naypyidaw" title="Naypyidaw">Naypyidaw</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-3"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup> By 15 March 2021 the military leadership continued to extend martial law into more parts of Yangon, while security forces killed 38 people in a single day of violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reaction">Reaction</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3472" data-file-width="4624" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg/220px-We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg/330px-We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg/440px-We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:We_want_our_leader_free_Daw_Aung_San_Su_Kyi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesters against the military coup in Myanmar</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2021%E2%80%932022_Myanmar_protests" title="2021â2022 Myanmar protests">2021â2022 Myanmar protests</a></div>
<p>By the second day of the coup, thousands of protesters were marching in the streets of the nation's largest city, and commercial capital, <a href="/wiki/Yangon" title="Yangon">Yangon</a>, and other protests erupted nationwide, largely halting commerce and transportation. Despite the military's arrests and killings of protesters, the first weeks of the coup found growing public participation, including groups of civil servants, teachers, students, workers, monks and religious leaders â even normally disaffected ethnic minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tens_of_thousands_2021_02_07_irrawaddy_com_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-tens_of_thousands_2021_02_07_irrawaddy_com-149">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-4"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>The coup was immediately condemned by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary_General" title="United Nations Secretary General">United Nations Secretary General</a>, and leaders of democratic nations â including the United States President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a>, western European political leaders, Southeast Asian democracies, and others around the world, who demanded or urged release of the captive leaders, and an immediate return to democratic rule in Myanmar. The U.S. threatened sanctions on the military and its leaders, including a "freeze" of US$1 billion of their assets in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-5"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> refrained from criticizing the military coup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> The representatives of Russia and China had conferred with the Tatmadaw leader Gen. Hlaing just days before the coup<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-red_carpet_2021_01_25_irrawaddy_com_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-red_carpet_2021_01_25_irrawaddy_com-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vladimir_putin_2021_02_14_thetimes_co_uk_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-vladimir_putin_2021_02_14_thetimes_co_uk-155">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-china_will_give_2021_01_12_reuters_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-china_will_give_2021_01_12_reuters-156">[154]</a></sup> Their possible complicity angered civilian protesters in Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhrc_china_russia_2021_02_13_irrawaddy_com_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-unhrc_china_russia_2021_02_13_irrawaddy_com-157">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-protesters_2021_02_17_au_news_yahoo_com_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-protesters_2021_02_17_au_news_yahoo_com-158">[156]</a></sup> However, both of those nations refrained from blocking a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> resolution calling for the release of Aung San Suu Kyi and the other detained leaders<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc_148-2"><a href="#cite_note-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-6"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup> â a position shared by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights">United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-7"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>International development and aid partners â business, non-governmental, and governmental â hinted at suspension of partnerships with Myanmar. Banks were closed and <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">Social media</a> communications platforms, including <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, removed Tatmadaw postings. Protesters appeared at Myanmar embassies in foreign countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc_148-3"><a href="#cite_note-teachers_join_2021_02_05_bbc-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com_145-8"><a href="#cite_note-myanmar_coup_2021_02_21_nikkei_com-145">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Myanmar" title="Geography of Myanmar">Geography of Myanmar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1128" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg/300px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg/450px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg/600px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_MMR_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Myanmar map of KÃ¶ppen climate classification.</div></div></div>
<p>Myanmar has a total area of 678,500 square kilometres (262,000Â sqÂ mi). It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/9th_parallel_north" title="9th parallel north">9Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/29th_parallel_north" title="29th parallel north">29Â°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/92nd_meridian_east" title="92nd meridian east">92Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/102nd_meridian_east" title="102nd meridian east">102Â°E</a>. Myanmar is bordered in the northwest by the <a href="/wiki/Chittagong_Division" title="Chittagong Division">Chittagong Division</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mizoram" title="Mizoram">Mizoram</a>, Manipur, <a href="/wiki/Nagaland" title="Nagaland">Nagaland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arunachal_Pradesh" title="Arunachal Pradesh">Arunachal Pradesh</a> states of India. Its north and northeast border is with the <a href="/wiki/Tibet_Autonomous_Region" title="Tibet Autonomous Region">Tibet Autonomous Region</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">Yunnan</a> for a Sino-Myanmar border total of 2,185Â km (1,358Â mi). It is bounded by <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> to the southeast. Myanmar has 1,930Â km (1,200Â mi) of contiguous coastline along the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andaman_Sea" title="Andaman Sea">Andaman Sea</a> to the southwest and the south, which forms one quarter of its total perimeter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the north, the <a href="/wiki/Hengduan_Mountains" title="Hengduan Mountains">Hengduan Mountains</a> form the border with China. <a href="/wiki/Hkakabo_Razi" title="Hkakabo Razi">Hkakabo Razi</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Kachin_State" title="Kachin State">Kachin State</a>, at an elevation of 5,881 metres (19,295Â ft), is the highest point in Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> Many mountain ranges, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rakhine_Yoma" title="Rakhine Yoma">Rakhine Yoma</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bago_Yoma" title="Bago Yoma">Bago Yoma</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shan_Hills" title="Shan Hills">Shan Hills</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tenasserim_Hills" title="Tenasserim Hills">Tenasserim Hills</a> exist within Myanmar, all of which run north-to-south from the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myathan_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-myathan-160">[158]</a></sup> The mountain chains divide Myanmar's three river systems, which are the <a href="/wiki/Irrawaddy_River" title="Irrawaddy River">Irrawaddy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salween_River" title="Salween River">Salween (Thanlwin)</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sittaung_River" title="Sittaung River">Sittaung</a> rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myatthein_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-myatthein-161">[159]</a></sup> The Irrawaddy River, Myanmar's longest river at nearly 2,170 kilometres (1,348Â mi), flows into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Martaban" title="Gulf of Martaban">Gulf of Martaban</a>. Fertile plains exist in the valleys between the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_chain" title="Mountain chain">mountain chains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myathan_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-myathan-160">[158]</a></sup> The majority of Myanmar's population lives in the <a href="/wiki/Irrawaddy_River" title="Irrawaddy River">Irrawaddy</a> valley, which is situated between the <a href="/wiki/Arakan_Mountains" title="Arakan Mountains">Rakhine Yoma</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shan_Hills" title="Shan Hills">Shan Plateau</a>.
</p>

<p>Myanmar is divided into seven states (<span title="Burmese-language text"><span lang="my">áá¼ááºáááº</span></span>) and seven regions (<span title="Burmese-language text"><span lang="my">áá­á¯ááºá¸áá±ááá¼á®á¸</span></span>), formerly called divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> Regions are predominantly Bamar (that is, mainly inhabited by Myanmar's dominant ethnic group). States, in essence, are regions that are home to particular ethnic minorities. The administrative divisions are further subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Myanmar" title="Districts of Myanmar">districts</a>, which are further subdivided into townships, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ward_(country_subdivision)" title="Ward (country subdivision)">wards</a>, and villages.
</p><p>Below are the number of districts, townships, cities/towns, wards, village groups and villages in each division and state of Myanmar as of 31 December 2001:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Myanmar" title="Climate of Myanmar">Climate of Myanmar</a></div>
<p>Much of the country lies between the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>. It lies in the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> region of Asia, with its coastal regions receiving over 5,000Â mm (196.9Â in) of rain annually. Annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">rainfall</a> in the <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">delta</a> region is approximately 2,500Â mm (98.4Â in), while average annual rainfall in the dry zone in central Myanmar is less than 1,000Â mm (39.4Â in). The northern regions of Myanmar are the coolest, with average temperatures of 21Â Â°C (70Â Â°F). Coastal and delta regions have an average maximum temperature of 32Â Â°C (89.6Â Â°F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myatthein_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-myatthein-161">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>Previously and currently analysed data, as well as future projections on changes caused by climate change predict serious consequences to development for all economic, productive, social, and environmental sectors in Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-164">[162]</a></sup> In order to combat the hardships ahead and do its part to help <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">combat climate change</a> Myanmar has displayed interest in expanding its use of renewable energy and lowering its level of carbon emissions. Groups involved in helping Myanmar with the transition and move forward include the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">UN Environment Programme</a>, Myanmar Climate Change Alliance, and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Natural_Resources_and_Environmental_Conservation_(Myanmar)" title="Ministry of Natural Resources and Environmental Conservation (Myanmar)">Ministry of Natural Resources and Environmental Conservation</a> which directed in producing the final draft of the Myanmar national climate change policy that was presented to various sectors of the Myanmar government for review.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-165">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2015, it was announced that the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and Myanmar would enter a full partnership framework aimed to better access to electricity and other basic services for about six million people and expected to benefit three million pregnant woman and children through improved health services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-166">[164]</a></sup> Acquired funding and proper planning has allowed Myanmar to better prepare for the impacts of climate change by enacting programs which teach its people new farming methods, rebuild its infrastructure with materials resilient to natural disasters, and transition various sectors towards reducing greenhouse gas emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-167">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Myanmar" title="Wildlife of Myanmar">Wildlife of Myanmar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3200" data-file-width="4800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg/220px-Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg/330px-Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg/440px-Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kaw_Gon_towards_Shwe_Kyar_Pwint.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The limestone landscape of <a href="/wiki/Kayin_State" title="Kayin State">Kayin State</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Myanmar" title="Deforestation in Myanmar">Deforestation in Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Myanmar" title="List of protected areas of Myanmar">List of protected areas of Myanmar</a></div>
<p>Myanmar is a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiverse</a> country with more than 16,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plants" title="Plants">plant</a>, 314 <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammal</a>, 1131 <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">bird</a>, 293 <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptile</a>, and 139 <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibian</a> species, and 64 terrestrial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecosystems" title="Ecosystems">ecosystems</a> including tropical and subtropical vegetation, seasonally inundated wetlands, shoreline and tidal systems, and alpine ecosystems. Myanmar houses some of the largest intact natural ecosystems in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, but the remaining ecosystems are under threat from land use intensification and over-exploitation. According to the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List_of_Ecosystems" title="IUCN Red List of Ecosystems">IUCN Red List of Ecosystems</a> categories and criteria more than a third of Myanmar's land area has been converted to <a href="/wiki/Anthropogenic_biome" title="Anthropogenic biome">anthropogenic ecosystems</a> over the last 2â3 centuries, and nearly half of its ecosystems are threatened. Despite large gaps in information for some ecosystems, there is a large potential to develop a comprehensive <a href="/wiki/PAN_Parks" title="PAN Parks">protected area network</a> that protects its terrestrial biodiversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>Myanmar continues to perform badly in the global <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a> (EPI) with an overall ranking of 153 out of 180 countries in 2016; among the worst in the <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a> region, only ahead of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. The EPI was established in 2001 by the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> as a global gauge to measure how well individual countries perform in implementing the United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>. The environmental areas where Myanmar performs worst (i.e. highest ranking) are <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air quality</a> (174), health impacts of <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues" title="Environmental issues">environmental issues</a> (143) and <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitat</a> (142). Myanmar performs best (i.e. lowest ranking) in <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_fishing" title="Environmental impact of fishing">environmental impacts of fisheries</a> (21) but with declining <a href="/wiki/Fish_stocks" title="Fish stocks">fish stocks</a>. Despite several issues, Myanmar also ranks 64 and scores very good (i.e. a high percentage of 93.73%) in environmental effects of the agricultural industry because of an excellent management of the <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_cycle" title="Nitrogen cycle">nitrogen cycle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> Myanmar is one of the most highly vulnerable countries to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>; this poses a number of social, political, economic and foreign policy challenges to the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.18/10, ranking it 49th globally out of 172 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-172">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>Myanmar's slow economic growth has contributed to the preservation of much of its environment and ecosystems. <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">Forests</a>, including dense tropical growth and valuable <a href="/wiki/Teak" title="Teak">teak</a> in lower Myanmar, cover over 49% of the country, including areas of <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">bamboo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hopea_odorata" title="Hopea odorata">ironwood</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Magnolia_champaca" title="Magnolia champaca">Magnolia champaca</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">Coconut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Areca_catechu" title="Areca catechu">betel palm</a> and rubber have been introduced. In the <a href="/wiki/Highland" title="Highland">highlands</a> of the north, oak, pine and various rhododendrons cover much of the land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup>
</p><p>Heavy logging since the new 1995 forestry law went into effect has seriously reduced forest area and wildlife habitat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> The lands along the coast support all varieties of tropical fruits and once had large areas of <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Coast_mangroves" title="Myanmar Coast mangroves">mangroves</a> although much of the protective mangroves have disappeared. In much of central Myanmar (the dry zone), <a href="/wiki/Vegetation" title="Vegetation">vegetation</a> is sparse and stunted.
</p><p>Typical jungle animals, particularly <a href="/wiki/Tiger" title="Tiger">tigers</a>, occur sparsely in Myanmar. In upper Myanmar, there are <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_water_buffalo" title="Wild water buffalo">wild water buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clouded_leopard" title="Clouded leopard">clouded leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelope</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephants</a>, which are also tamed or bred in captivity for use as work animals, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Wood_industry" title="Wood industry">lumber industry</a>. Smaller mammals are also numerous, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Gibbon" title="Gibbon">gibbons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">monkeys</a> to <a href="/wiki/Pteropus" title="Pteropus">flying foxes</a>. The abundance of <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a> is notable with over 800 species, including <a href="/wiki/Rose-ringed_parakeet" title="Rose-ringed parakeet">parrots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myna" title="Myna">myna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peafowl" title="Peafowl">peafowl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_junglefowl" title="Red junglefowl">red junglefowl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ploceidae" title="Ploceidae">weaverbirds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crow" title="Crow">crows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heron" title="Heron">herons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barn_owl" title="Barn owl">barn owl</a>. Among reptile species there are <a href="/wiki/Crocodile" title="Crocodile">crocodiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gecko" title="Gecko">geckos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobra" title="Cobra">cobras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burmese_python" title="Burmese python">Burmese pythons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turtle" title="Turtle">turtles</a>. Hundreds of species of freshwater fish are wide-ranging, plentiful and are very important food sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output
