style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Head of Government, Deputy Head of Government, and acting Head of State
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Min_Aung_Hlaing" title="Min Aung Hlaing">Min Aung Hlaing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Myanmar" title="Prime Minister of Myanmar">Prime Minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_State_Administration_Council" title="Chairman of the State Administration Council">Chairman of the State Administration Council</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Soe_Win_(general)" title="Soe Win (general)">Soe Win</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_Myanmar" title="Deputy Prime Minister of Myanmar">Deputy Prime Minister</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vice_Chairman_of_the_State_Administration_Council" title="Vice Chairman of the State Administration Council">Vice Chairman of the State Administration Council</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myint_Swe_(general)" title="Myint Swe (general)">Myint Swe</a>, acting <a href="/wiki/President_of_Myanmar" title="President of Myanmar">President of Myanmar</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div>
<p>Myanmar operates <i>de jure</i> as a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assembly-independent" title="Assembly-independent">assembly-independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> under its <a href="/wiki/2008_Constitution_of_Myanmar" title="2008 Constitution of Myanmar">2008 constitution</a>. But in February 2021, the civilian government led by <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>, was deposed by the <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Tatmadaw</a>. In February 2021, <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Myanmar military</a> declared a one-year state emergency and First Vice President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myint_Swe_(general)" title="Myint Swe (general)">Myint Swe</a> became the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Myanmar" title="President of Myanmar">Acting President of Myanmar</a> and handed the power to the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-Chief_of_Defence_Services" title="Commander-in-Chief of Defence Services">Commander-in-Chief of Defence Services</a> <a href="/wiki/Min_Aung_Hlaing" title="Min Aung Hlaing">Min Aung Hlaing</a> and he assumed the role <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_State_Administration_Council" title="Chairman of the State Administration Council">Chairman of the State Administration Council</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Myanmar" title="Prime Minister of Myanmar">Prime Minister</a>. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Myanmar" title="President of Myanmar">President of Myanmar</a> acts as the <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a> <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_State_Administration_Council" title="Chairman of the State Administration Council">Chairman of the State Administration Council</a> acts as the <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg/220px-Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg/330px-Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg/440px-Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Myanmar-Lower-House-Parliament.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Union" title="Assembly of the Union">Assembly of the Union</a> (Pyidaungsu Hluttaw)</div></div></div>
<p>The constitution of Myanmar, its third since independence, was drafted by its military rulers and published in September 2008. The country is governed as a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral legislature</a> (with an executive <a href="/wiki/President_of_Myanmar" title="President of Myanmar">president</a> accountable to the legislature), with 25% of the legislators appointed by the military and the rest elected in general elections.
</p><p>The legislature, called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Union" title="Assembly of the Union">Assembly of the Union</a>, is bicameral and made up of two houses: the 224-seat upper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Nationalities" title="House of Nationalities">House of Nationalities</a> and the 440-seat lower <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Myanmar)" title="House of Representatives (Myanmar)">House of Representatives</a>. The upper house consists 168 members who are directly elected and 56 who are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Burmese Armed Forces</a>. The lower house consists of 330 members who are directly elected and 110 who are appointed by the armed forces.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span></h3>
<p>The major political parties are the <a href="/wiki/National_League_for_Democracy" title="National League for Democracy">National League for Democracy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Union_Solidarity_and_Development_Party" title="Union Solidarity and Development Party">Union Solidarity and Development Party</a>.
</p><p>Myanmar's army-drafted constitution was approved in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Burmese_constitutional_referendum" title="2008 Burmese constitutional referendum">referendum</a> in May 2008. The results, 92.4% of the 22 million voters with an official turnout of 99%, are considered suspect by many international observers and by the National League of Democracy with reports of widespread <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">fraud</a>, ballot stuffing, and voter intimidation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_Myanmar_general_election" title="2010 Myanmar general election">elections of 2010</a> resulted in a victory for the military-backed Union Solidarity and Development Party. Various foreign observers questioned the fairness of the elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> One criticism of the election was that only government-sanctioned political parties were allowed to contest in it and the popular <a href="/wiki/National_League_for_Democracy" title="National League for Democracy">National League for Democracy</a> was declared illegal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardianASSK_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardianASSK-181">[179]</a></sup> However, immediately following the elections, the government ended the house arrest of the democracy advocate and leader of the National League for Democracy, <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> and her ability to move freely around the country is considered an important test of the military's movement toward more openness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardianASSK_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardianASSK-181">[179]</a></sup> After unexpected <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%932015_Myanmar_political_reforms" title="2011â2015 Myanmar political reforms">reforms in 2011</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_League_for_Democracy" title="National League for Democracy">NLD</a> senior leaders have decided to register as a political party and to field candidates in future by-elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup>
</p><p>Myanmar's political history is underlined by its struggle to establish democratic structures amidst conflicting factions. This political transition from a closely held military rule to a free democratic system is widely believed to be determining the future of Myanmar. The resounding victory of <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>'s National League for Democracy in the 2015 general election raised hope for a successful culmination of this transition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup>
</p><p>Myanmar rates as a corrupt nation on the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> with a rank of 130th out of 180 countries worldwide, with 1st being least corrupt, as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Myanmar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Myanmar" title="Foreign relations of Myanmar">Foreign relations of Myanmar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_meets_with_Thein_Sein_at_Burma_Parliament_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Myanmar President Thein Sein meets US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yangon" title="Yangon">Yangon</a>, 2012</div></div></div>
<p>Though the country's foreign relations, particularly with <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western nations</a>, have historically been strained, the situation has markedly improved since the reforms following the 2010 elections. After years of diplomatic isolation and economic and military sanctions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> the United States relaxed curbs on foreign aid to Myanmar in November 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinton_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clinton-119">[117]</a></sup> and announced the resumption of diplomatic relations on 13 January 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> has placed sanctions on Myanmar, including an <a href="/wiki/Arms_embargo" title="Arms embargo">arms embargo</a>, cessation of <a href="/wiki/Trade_preference" title="Trade preference">trade preferences</a>, and suspension of all aid with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian aid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U_Thant_(1963).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1353" data-file-width="1013" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U_Thant_%281963%29.jpg/170px-U_Thant_%281963%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U_Thant_%281963%29.jpg/255px-U_Thant_%281963%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U_Thant_%281963%29.jpg/340px-U_Thant_%281963%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U_Thant_(1963).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a> (1961â1971)</div></div></div>
<p>Sanctions imposed by the United States and European countries against the former military government, coupled with boycotts and other direct pressure on corporations by supporters of the democracy movement, have resulted in the withdrawal from the country of most U.S. and many European companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> On 13 April 2012, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> called for the economic sanctions on Myanmar to be suspended in the wake of the pro-democracy party gaining 43 seats out of a possible 45 in the 2012 by-elections with the party leader, <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> becoming a member of the Burmese parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite Western isolation, Asian corporations have generally remained willing to continue investing in the country and to initiate new investments, particularly in natural resource extraction. The country has close relations with neighbouring India and China with several Indian and Chinese companies operating in the country. Under India's <a href="/wiki/Look_East_policy_(India)" title="Look East policy (India)">Look East policy</a>, fields of co-operation between India and Myanmar include <a href="/wiki/Remote_sensing" title="Remote sensing">remote sensing</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> oil and gas exploration,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> information technology,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> hydropower<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> and construction of ports and buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, India suspended military aid to Myanmar over the issue of human rights abuses by the ruling junta, although it has preserved extensive commercial ties, which provide the regime with much-needed revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> The thaw in relations began on 28 November 2011, when Belarusian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Myasnikovich" title="Mikhail Myasnikovich">Mikhail Myasnikovich</a> and his wife Ludmila arrived in the capital, Naypyidaw, the same day as the country received a visit by U.S. Secretary of State Hillary Clinton, who also met with pro-democracy opposition leader Aung San Suu Kyi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> International relations progress indicators continued in September 2012 when Aung San Suu Kyi visited the United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> followed by Myanmar's reformist president visit to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, Thein Sein became the first Myanmar president to visit the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> in 47 years; the last Burmese leader to visit the White House was <a href="/wiki/Ne_Win" title="Ne Win">Ne Win</a> in September 1966. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> praised the former general for political and economic reforms and the cessation of tensions between Myanmar and the United States. Political activists objected to the visit because of concerns over human rights abuses in Myanmar, but Obama assured Thein Sein that Myanmar will receive U.S. support. The two leaders discussed the release of more political prisoners, the institutionalisation of political reform and the rule of law, and ending ethnic conflict in Myanmarâthe two governments agreed to sign a <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_trade" title="Bilateral trade">bilateral trade</a> and investment framework agreement on 21 May 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2013, Myanmar held its first ever summit, the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> on East Asia 2013. A regional spinoff of the annual <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Davos" title="Davos">Davos</a>, Switzerland, the summit was held on 5â7 June and attended by 1,200 participants, including 10 heads of state, 12 ministers and 40 senior directors from around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_forces_of_Myanmar" title="Armed forces of Myanmar">Armed forces of Myanmar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="705" data-file-width="1110" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg/220px-Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg/330px-Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg/440px-Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Myanmar_Air_Force_MiG-29_MRD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Air_Force" title="Myanmar Air Force">Myanmar Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan_MiG-29" title="Mikoyan MiG-29">Mikoyan MiG-29</a> multirole fighter</div></div></div>
<p>Myanmar has received extensive military aid from China in the past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup>
Myanmar has been a member of ASEAN since 1997. Though it gave up its turn to hold the ASEAN chair and host the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Summit" title="ASEAN Summit">ASEAN Summit</a> in 2006, it chaired the forum and hosted the summit in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> In November 2008, Myanmar's political situation with neighbouring Bangladesh became tense as they began searching for natural gas in a disputed block of the Bay of Bengal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup> Controversy surrounding the Rohingya population also remains an issue between Bangladesh and Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup>
</p><p>Myanmar's armed forces are known as the <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Tatmadaw</a>, which numbers 488,000. The Tatmadaw comprises the <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Army" title="Myanmar Army">Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Navy" title="Myanmar Navy">Navy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Air_Force" title="Myanmar Air Force">Air Force</a>. The country <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">ranked twelfth</a> in the world for its number of active troops in service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCGUB_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-NCGUB-32">[30]</a></sup> The military is very influential in Myanmar, with all top cabinet and ministry posts usually held by military officials. Official figures for military spending are not available. Estimates vary widely because of uncertain exchange rates, but Myanmar's military forces' expenses are high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup> Myanmar imports most of its weapons from Russia, Ukraine, China and India.
</p><p>Myanmar is building a research <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> near <a href="/wiki/Pyin_Oo_Lwin" title="Pyin Oo Lwin">Pyin Oo Lwin</a> with help from Russia. It is one of the signatories of the nuclear <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">non-proliferation</a> pact since 1992 and a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> (IAEA) since 1957. The military junta had informed the IAEA in September 2000 of its intention to construct the reactor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup> In 2010 as part of the Wikileaks leaked cables, Myanmar was suspected of using North Korean construction teams to build a fortified surface-to-air missile facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup> As of 2019, the United States <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Arms_Control,_Verification,_and_Compliance" title="Bureau of Arms Control, Verification, and Compliance">Bureau of Arms Control</a> assessed that Myanmar is not in violation of its obligations under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons">Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> but that the Myanmar government had a history of non-transparency on its nuclear programs and aims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACVC_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACVC-211">[209]</a></sup>
</p><p>Until 2005, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> annually adopted a detailed resolution about the situation in Myanmar by consensus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN-5483030_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN-5483030-212">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup> But in 2006 a divided United Nations General Assembly voted through a resolution that strongly called upon the government of Myanmar to end its systematic violations of human rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup> In January 2007, Russia and China vetoed a draft resolution before the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[215]</a></sup> calling on the government of Myanmar to respect human rights and begin a democratic transition. South Africa also voted against the resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[216]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_and_internal_conflicts">Human rights and internal conflicts</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Myanmar" title="Human rights in Myanmar">Human rights in Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Internal_conflict_in_Myanmar" title="Internal conflict in Myanmar">Internal conflict in Myanmar</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Undue_weight_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section may <b>lend <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Due_and_undue_weight" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">undue weight</a> to certain ideas, incidents, or controversies</b>. Please help to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:STRUCTURE" title="Wikipedia:STRUCTURE">create a more balanced presentation</a>. Discuss and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Dispute_resolution" title="Wikipedia:Dispute resolution">resolve</a> this issue before removing this message.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2020</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2938" data-file-width="1324" decoding="async" height="399" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png/180px-Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png/270px-Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png/360px-Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Armed_conflict_zones_in_Myanmar.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of conflict zones in Myanmar. <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Myanmar" title="Administrative divisions of Myanmar">States</a> and regions affected by fighting during and after 1995 are highlighted in yellow.</div></div></div>
<p>There is consensus that the former military regime in Myanmar (1962â2010) was one of the world's most repressive and abusive regimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[218]</a></sup> In November 2012, <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Power" title="Samantha Power">Samantha Power</a>, Barack Obama's Special Assistant to the President on Human Rights, wrote on the White House blog in advance of the president's visit that "Serious human rights abuses against civilians in several regions continue, including against women and children."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShanVsGovt_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-ShanVsGovt-105">[103]</a></sup> Members of the United Nations and major international human rights organisations have issued repeated and consistent reports of widespread and systematic human rights violations in Myanmar. The United Nations General Assembly has repeatedly<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup> called on the Burmese military junta to respect human rights and in November 2009 the General Assembly adopted a resolution "strongly condemning the ongoing systematic violations of human rights and fundamental freedoms" and calling on the Burmese military regime "to take urgent measures to put an end to violations of international human rights and humanitarian law."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[220]</a></sup>
</p><p>International human rights organisations including <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[221]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[222]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">American Association for the Advancement of Science</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[223]</a></sup> have repeatedly documented and condemned widespread human rights violations in Myanmar. The <i>Freedom in the World 2011</i> report by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> notes, "The military junta hasÂ ... suppressed nearly all basic rights; and committed human rights abuses with impunity." In July 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Assistance_Association_for_Political_Prisoners" title="Assistance Association for Political Prisoners">Assistance Association for Political Prisoners</a> indicated that there were approximately 100 political prisoners being held in Burmese prisons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mmtimes1_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-mmtimes1-226">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irrawaddy1_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-irrawaddy1-227">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup> Evidence gathered by a British researcher was published in 2005 regarding the extermination or "Burmisation" of certain ethnic minorities, such as the <a href="/wiki/Karen_people" title="Karen people">Karen</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karenni" title="Karenni">Karenni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shan_people" title="Shan people">Shan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[228]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="859" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg/220px-Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg/330px-Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg/440px-Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mae_La_refugee_camp2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mae_La_refugee_camp" title="Mae La refugee camp">Mae La camp</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tak_Province" title="Tak Province">Tak</a>, Thailand, one of the largest of nine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a> camps in Thailand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[229]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Based on the evidence gathered by Amnesty photographs and video of the ongoing armed conflict between the Myanmar military and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arakan_Army_(Kachin_State)" title="Arakan Army (Kachin State)">Arakan Army</a> (AA), attacks escalated on civilians in Rakhine State. Ming Yu Hah, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>'s Deputy Regional Director for Campaigns said, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> must urgently refer the situation in Myanmar to the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup> The military is notorious for rampant use of sexual violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHR_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNHR-15">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_soldiers">Child soldiers</span></h4>
<p>Child soldiers were reported in 2012 to have played a major part in the Burmese Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-233">[231]</a></sup> <i>The Independent</i> reported in June 2012 that "Children are being sold as conscripts into the Burmese military for as little as $40 and a bag of rice or a can of petrol."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> The UN's Special Representative of the Secretary-General for Children and Armed Conflict, <a href="/wiki/Radhika_Coomaraswamy" title="Radhika Coomaraswamy">Radhika Coomaraswamy</a>, who stepped down from her position a week later, met representatives of the government of Myanmar in July 2012 and stated that she hoped the government's signing of an action plan would "signal a transformation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[233]</a></sup> In September 2012, the Myanmar Armed Forces released 42 child soldiers, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> met with representatives of the government as well as the <a href="/wiki/Kachin_Independence_Army" title="Kachin Independence Army">Kachin Independence Army</a> to secure the release of more child soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[234]</a></sup> According to Samantha Power, a U.S. delegation raised the issue of child soldiers with the government in October 2012. However, she did not comment on the government's progress towards reform in this area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShanVsGovt_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-ShanVsGovt-105">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery_and_human_trafficking">Slavery and human trafficking</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking_in_Myanmar" title="Sex trafficking in Myanmar">Sex trafficking in Myanmar</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" title="Unfree labour">Forced labour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">child labour</a> are common in Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[236]</a></sup> In 2007 the international movement to defend women's human rights issues in Myanmar was said to be gaining speed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[237]</a></sup> Human trafficking happens mostly to women who are unemployed and have low incomes. They are mainly targeted or deceived by brokers into making them believe that better opportunities and wages exist for them abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup> In 2017, the government reported investigating 185 trafficking cases. The government of Burma makes little effort to eliminate human trafficking. Burmese armed forces compel troops to acquire labour and supplies from local communities. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> reported that both the government and <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Tatmadaw</a> were complicit in sex and labour trafficking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[239]</a></sup> Women and girls from all <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_in_Myanmar" title="List of ethnic groups in Myanmar">ethnic groups</a> and foreigners have been victims of sex trafficking in Myanmar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-233">[231]</a></sup> They are forced into prostitution, marriages, and or pregnancies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[241]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Genocide_allegations_and_crimes_against_Rohingya_people">Genocide allegations and crimes against Rohingya people</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_(8280610831).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_%288280610831%29.jpg/220px-Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_%288280610831%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_%288280610831%29.jpg/330px-Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_%288280610831%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_%288280610831%29.jpg/440px-Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_%288280610831%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Displaced_Rohingya_people_in_Rakhine_State_(8280610831).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Displaced <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya people</a> of Myanmar<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[242]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[243]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_conflict" title="Rohingya conflict">Rohingya conflict</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_Myanmar_anti-Muslim_riots" title="2013 Myanmar anti-Muslim riots">2013 Myanmar anti-Muslim riots</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_genocide" title="Rohingya genocide">Rohingya genocide</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya people</a> have consistently faced human rights abuses by the Burmese regime that has refused to acknowledge them as Burmese citizens (despite some of them having lived in Burma for over three generations)âthe Rohingya have been denied Burmese citizenship since the enactment of a <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_nationality_law" title="Myanmar nationality law">1982 citizenship law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rohingya_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-rohingya-246">[244]</a></sup> The law created three categories of citizenship: citizenship, associate citizenship, and naturalised citizenship. Citizenship is given to those who belong to one of the national races such as Kachin, Kayah (Karenni), Karen, Chin, Burman, Mon, Rakhine, Shan, Kaman, or Zerbadee. Associate citizenship is given to those who cannot prove their ancestors settled in Myanmar before 1823 but can prove they have one grandparent, or pre-1823 ancestor, who was a citizen of another country, as well as people who applied for citizenship in 1948 and qualified then by those laws. Naturalised citizenship is only given to those who have at least one parent with one of these types of Burmese citizenship or can provide "conclusive evidence" that their parents entered and resided in Burma prior to independence in 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[245]</a></sup> The Burmese regime has attempted to forcibly expel Rohingya and bring in non-Rohingyas to replace them<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-South_East_Asia_pg._342_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-South_East_Asia_pg._342-248">[246]</a></sup>âthis policy has resulted in the expulsion of approximately half of the 800,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[247]</a></sup> Rohingya from Burma, while the Rohingya people have been described as "among the world's least wanted"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[248]</a></sup> and "one of the world's most persecuted minorities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-South_East_Asia_pg._342_248-1"><a href="#cite_note-South_East_Asia_pg._342-248">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[249]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[250]</a></sup> But the origin of the "most persecuted minority" statement is unclear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[251]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rohingya are not allowed to travel without official permission, are banned from owning land, and are required to sign a commitment to have no more than two children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rohingya_246-1"><a href="#cite_note-rohingya-246">[244]</a></sup> As of July 2012, the Myanmar government does not include the Rohingya minority groupâclassified as <a href="/wiki/Statelessness" title="Statelessness">stateless</a> Bengali Muslims from Bangladesh since 1982âon the government's list of more than 130 ethnic races and, therefore, the government states that they have no claim to Myanmar citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[252]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007 German professor <a href="/wiki/Bassam_Tibi" title="Bassam Tibi">Bassam Tibi</a> suggested that the Rohingya conflict may be driven by an Islamist political agenda to impose religious laws,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[253]</a></sup> while non-religious causes have also been raised, such as a lingering resentment over the violence that occurred during the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Burma" title="Japanese occupation of Burma">Japanese occupation of Burma</a> in World War IIâduring this time period the British allied themselves with the Rohingya<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[254]</a></sup> and fought against the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Burma" title="State of Burma">puppet government of Burma</a> (composed mostly of Bamar Japanese) that helped to establish the <a href="/wiki/Tatmadaw" title="Tatmadaw">Tatmadaw</a> military organisation that remains in power except for a 5-year lapse in 2016 - 2021.
</p><p>Since the democratic transition began in 2011, there has been continuous violence as 280 people have been killed and 140,000 forced to flee from their homes in the Rakhine state in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[255]</a></sup> A UN envoy reported in March 2013 that unrest had re-emerged between Myanmar's <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslim</a> communities, with violence spreading to towns that are located closer to Yangon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[256]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_reforms">Government reforms</span></h4>
<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crisis_Group" title="Crisis Group">Crisis Group</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[257]</a></sup> since Myanmar transitioned to a new government in August 2011, the country's human rights record has been improving. Previously giving Myanmar its lowest rating of 7, the 2012 <i>Freedom in the World</i> report also notes improvement, giving Myanmar a 6 for improvements in civil liberties and political rights, the release of political prisoners, and a loosening of restrictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[258]</a></sup> In 2013, Myanmar improved yet again, receiving a score of 5 in civil liberties and 6 in political freedoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[259]</a></sup>
</p><p>The government has assembled a <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_National_Human_Rights_Commission" title="Myanmar National Human Rights Commission">National Human Rights Commission</a> that consists of 15 members from various backgrounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[260]</a></sup> Several activists in exile, including Thee Lay Thee Anyeint members, have returned to Myanmar after President Thein Sein's invitation to expatriates to return home to work for national development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[261]</a></sup> In an address to the United Nations Security Council on 22 September 2011, Myanmar's Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Wunna_Maung_Lwin" title="Wunna Maung Lwin">Wunna Maung Lwin</a> confirmed the government's intention to release prisoners in the near future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[262]</a></sup>
</p><p>
The government has also relaxed reporting laws, but these remain highly restrictive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[263]</a></sup> In September 2011, several banned websites, including YouTube, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Voice_of_Burma" title="Democratic Voice of Burma">Democratic Voice of Burma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a>, were unblocked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[264]</a></sup> A 2011 report by the <a href="/wiki/Hauser_Center_for_Nonprofit_Organizations" title="Hauser Center for Nonprofit Organizations">Hauser Center for Nonprofit Organizations</a> found that, while contact with the Myanmar government was constrained by donor restrictions, international humanitarian non-governmental organisations (NGOs) see opportunities for effective advocacy with government officials, especially at the local level. At the same time, international NGOs are mindful of the ethical quandary of how to work with the government without bolstering or appeasing it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_(John_Owens-VOA).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2549" data-file-width="4540" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_%28John_Owens-VOA%29.jpg/220px-Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_%28John_Owens-VOA%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_%28John_Owens-VOA%29.jpg/330px-Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_%28John_Owens-VOA%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_%28John_Owens-VOA%29.jpg/440px-Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_%28John_Owens-VOA%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kutupalong_Refugee_Camp_(John_Owens-VOA).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Rohingya refugee camp in Bangladesh</div></div></div>
<p>Following Thein Sein's first ever visit to the UK and a meeting with Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, the Myanmar president declared that all of his nation's political prisoners will be released by the end of 2013, in addition to a statement of support for the well-being of the Rohingya Muslim community. In a speech at <a href="/wiki/Chatham_House" title="Chatham House">Chatham House</a>, he revealed that "We [Myanmar government] are reviewing all cases. I guarantee to you that by the end of this year, there will be no prisoners of conscience in Myanmar.", in addition to expressing a desire to strengthen links between the UK and Myanmar's military forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[266]</a></sup>
</p><p>Homosexual acts are <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Myanmar" title="LGBT rights in Myanmar">illegal in Myanmar</a> and can be punishable by life imprisonment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Myanmar leader <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a> was accused of failing to protect Myanmar's <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Myanmar" title="Islam in Myanmar">Muslim</a> minority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[269]</a></sup> Since August 2017 <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="MÃ©decins Sans FrontiÃ¨res">Doctors Without Borders</a> have treated 113 Rohingya refugee females for sexual assault with all but one describing military assailants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[270]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Burma_Product_Exports_(2019).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Burma_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/290px-Burma_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Burma_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/435px-Burma_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Burma_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/580px-Burma_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Burma_Product_Exports_(2019).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Myanmar exports, 2019</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Myanmar" title="Economy of Myanmar">Economy of Myanmar</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Golden_Triangle_(Southeast_Asia)" title="Golden Triangle (Southeast Asia)">Golden Triangle (Southeast Asia)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Myanmar" title="Transport in Myanmar">Transport in Myanmar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oil_and_gas_industry_in_Myanmar" title="Oil and gas industry in Myanmar">Oil and gas industry in Myanmar</a></div>
<p>Myanmar's <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a> is one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fastest_growing_economies" title="Fastest growing economies">fastest growing economies</a> in the world with a nominal GDP of US$76.09 billion in 2019 and an estimated purchasing power adjusted GDP of US$327.629 billion in 2017 according to the World Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[271]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Synthesis_of_published_material" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag may be based upon an improper synthesis of sources. (June 2021)">improper synthesis?</span></a></i>]</sup> Foreigners are able to legally lease but not own property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aht_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-aht-274">[272]</a></sup> In December 2014, Myanmar set up its first stock exchange, the <a href="/wiki/Yangon_Stock_Exchange" title="Yangon Stock Exchange">Yangon Stock Exchange</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[273]</a></sup>
</p><p>The informal economy's share in Myanmar is one of the biggest in the world and is closely linked to corruption, smuggling and illegal trade activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[274]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[275]</a></sup> In addition, decades of civil war and unrest have contributed to Myanmar's current levels of poverty and lack of economic progress. Myanmar lacks adequate <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a>. Goods travel primarily across the Thai border (where most illegal drugs are exported) and along the Irrawaddy River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idea_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-idea-278">[276]</a></sup>
</p><p>Both China and India have attempted to strengthen ties with the government for economic benefit in the early 2010s. Many Western nations, including the United States and Canada, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, historically imposed investment and trade sanctions on Myanmar. The United States and European Union eased most of their sanctions in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[277]</a></sup> From May 2012 to February 2013, the United States began to lift its economic sanctions on Myanmar "in response to the historic reforms that have been taking place in that country."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[278]</a></sup> Foreign investment comes primarily from China, Singapore, the Philippines, South Korea, India, and Thailand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[279]</a></sup> The military has stakes in some major industrial corporations of the country (from oil production and consumer goods to transportation and tourism).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mccartan_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-mccartan-282">[280]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brady_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-brady-283">[281]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_history">Economic history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="4200" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg/220px-Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg/330px-Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg/440px-Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Myingyan_Railway_Station_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The trains are relatively slow in Myanmar. The railway trip from <a href="/wiki/Bagan" title="Bagan">Bagan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a> takes about 7.5 hours (179Â km).</div></div></div><p>Under the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> administration, the people of Burma were at the bottom of the social hierarchy, with <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">Europeans</a> at the top, Indians, Chinese, and Christianized minorities in the middle, and Buddhist Burmese at the bottom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-284">[282]</a></sup> Forcefully integrated into the world economy, Burma's economy grew by involving itself with extractive industries and <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crop</a> agriculture. However, much of the wealth was concentrated in the hands of Europeans. The country became the world's largest exporter of <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, mainly to European markets, while other colonies like India suffered mass starvation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[283]</a></sup> Being a follower free market principles, the British opened up the country to large-scale immigration with Rangoon exceeding New York City as the greatest immigration port in the world in the 1920s. Historian <a href="/wiki/Thant_Myint-U" title="Thant Myint-U">Thant Myint-U</a> states, "This was out of a total population of only 13 million; it was equivalent to the United Kingdom today taking 2 million people a year." By then, in most of Burma's largest cities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rangoon" title="Rangoon">Rangoon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akyab" title="Akyab">Akyab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pathein" title="Pathein">Bassein</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moulmein" title="Moulmein">Moulmein</a>, the Indian immigrants formed a majority of the population. The Burmese under British rule felt helpless, and reacted with a "racism that combined feelings of superiority and fear".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_284-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-284">[282]</a></sup>
</p><p>Crude oil production, an indigenous industry of <a href="/wiki/Yenangyaung" title="Yenangyaung">Yenangyaung</a>, was taken over by the British and put under <a href="/wiki/Burmah_Oil" title="Burmah Oil">Burmah Oil</a> monopoly. British Burma began exporting crude oil in 1853.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[284]</a></sup> European firms produced 75% of the world's teak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg-30">[28]</a></sup> The wealth was however, mainly concentrated in the hands of Europeans. In the 1930s, agricultural production fell dramatically as international rice prices declined and did not recover for several decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[285]</a></sup> During the Japanese invasion of Burma in World War II, the British followed a <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a> policy. They destroyed major government buildings, oil wells and mines that developed for tungsten (<a href="/wiki/Mawchi" title="Mawchi">Mawchi</a>), tin, lead and silver to keep them from the Japanese. Myanmar was bombed extensively by the Allies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>After independence, the country was in ruins with its major infrastructure completely destroyed. With the loss of India, Burma lost relevance and obtained independence from the British. After a parliamentary government was formed in 1948, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/U_Nu" title="U Nu">U Nu</a> embarked upon a policy of nationalisation and the state was declared the owner of all of the land in Burma. The government tried to implement an eight-year plan partly financed by injecting money into the economy, but this caused inflation to rise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[286]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1962_Burmese_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1962 Burmese coup d'Ã©tat">1962 coup d'Ã©tat</a> was followed by an economic scheme called the <a href="/wiki/Burmese_Way_to_Socialism" title="Burmese Way to Socialism">Burmese Way to Socialism</a>, a plan to nationalise all industries, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. While the economy continued to grow at a slower rate, the country eschewed a Western-oriented development model, and by the 1980s, was left behind capitalist powerhouses like <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> which were integrated with Western economies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[287]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ruin_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-ruin-86">[84]</a></sup> Myanmar asked for admittance to a <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">least developed country</a> status in 1987 to receive debt relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[288]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg/220px-Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg/330px-Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg/440px-Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rijstvelden_Myanmar_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rice is Myanmar's largest agricultural product.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Myanmar" title="Agriculture in Myanmar">Agriculture in Myanmar</a></div>
<p>The major agricultural product is <a href="/wiki/Rice_production_in_Myanmar" title="Rice production in Myanmar">rice</a>, which covers about 60% of the country's total cultivated land area. Rice accounts for 97% of total food grain production by weight. Through collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/International_Rice_Research_Institute" title="International Rice Research Institute">International Rice Research Institute</a> 52 modern rice varieties were released in the country between 1966 and 1997, helping increase national rice production to 14Â million tons in 1987 and to 19Â million tons in 1996. By 1988, modern varieties were planted on half of the country's ricelands, including 98 per cent of the irrigated areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[289]</a></sup> In 2008 rice production was estimated at 50 million tons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[290]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extractive_industries">Extractive industries</span></h3>
<p>Myanmar produces precious stones such as <a href="/wiki/Ruby" title="Ruby">rubies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sapphire" title="Sapphire">sapphires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pearl" title="Pearl">pearls</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jade" title="Jade">jade</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ruby" title="Ruby">Rubies</a> are the biggest earner; 90% of the world's rubies come from the country, whose red stones are prized for their purity and hue. Thailand buys the majority of the country's gems. Myanmar's "Valley of Rubies", the mountainous <a href="/wiki/Mogok_Township" title="Mogok Township">Mogok</a> area, 200Â km (120Â mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a>, is noted for its rare pigeon's blood rubies and blue sapphires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[291]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European</a> jewellery companies, including Bulgari, Tiffany and Cartier, refuse to import these stones based on reports of deplorable working conditions in the mines. <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> has encouraged a complete ban on the purchase of Burmese gems based on these reports and because nearly all profits go to the ruling junta, as the majority of mining activity in the country is government-run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[292]</a></sup> The government of Myanmar controls the gem trade by direct ownership or by joint ventures with private owners of mines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[293]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rare-earth_elements" title="Rare-earth elements">Rare-earth elements</a> are also a significant export, as Myanmar supplies around 10% of the world's rare earths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[294]</a></sup> Conflict in Kachin State has threatened the operations of its mines as of February 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[295]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[296]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other industries include agricultural goods, textiles, wood products, construction materials, gems, metals, oil and natural gas. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Myanmar_Engineering_Society&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Myanmar Engineering Society (page does not exist)">Myanmar Engineering Society</a> has identified at least 39 locations capable of geothermal power production and some of these hydrothermal reservoirs lie quite close to Yangon which is a significant underutilised resource for electrical production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[297]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Myanmar" title="Tourism in Myanmar">Tourism in Myanmar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tourists_in_Myanmar_(8397039153).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Tourists_in_Myanmar_%288397039153%29.jpg/220px-Tourists_in_Myanmar_%288397039153%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Tourists_in_Myanmar_%288397039153%29.jpg/330px-Tourists_in_Myanmar_%288397039153%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Tourists_in_Myanmar_%288397039153%29.jpg/440px-Tourists_in_Myanmar_%288397039153%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tourists_in_Myanmar_(8397039153).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tourists in Myanmar</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="4200" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg/220px-U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg/330px-U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg/440px-U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U_Bein_Bridge_Mandalay_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/U_Bein_Bridge" title="U Bein Bridge">U Bein Bridge</a> in Mandalay.</div></div></div>
<p>The government receives a significant percentage of the income of private-sector tourism services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[298]</a></sup> The most popular available tourist destinations in Myanmar include big cities such as <a href="/wiki/Yangon" title="Yangon">Yangon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandalay" title="Mandalay">Mandalay</a>; religious sites in <a href="/wiki/Mon_State" title="Mon State">Mon State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pindaya" title="Pindaya">Pindaya</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bago,_Burma" title="Bago, Burma">Bago</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hpa-An" title="Hpa-An">Hpa-An</a>; nature trails in <a href="/wiki/Inle_Lake" title="Inle Lake">Inle Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kengtung" title="Kengtung">Kengtung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Putao_District" title="Putao District">Putao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyin_Oo_Lwin" title="Pyin Oo Lwin">Pyin Oo Lwin</a>; ancient cities such as <a href="/wiki/Bagan" title="Bagan">Bagan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mrauk-U" title="Mrauk-U">Mrauk-U</a>; as well as beaches in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nabule&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nabule (page does not exist)">Nabule</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[299]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ngapali" title="Ngapali">Ngapali</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ngwe_Saung_Beach" title="Ngwe Saung Beach">Ngwe-Saung</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mergui" title="Mergui">Mergui</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[300]</a></sup> Nevertheless, much of the country is off-limits to tourists, and interactions between foreigners and the people of Myanmar, particularly in the border regions, are subject to police scrutiny. They are not to discuss politics with foreigners, under penalty of imprisonment and, in 2001, the Myanmar Tourism Promotion Board issued an order for local officials to protect tourists and limit "unnecessary contact" between foreigners and ordinary Burmese people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[301]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most common way for travellers to enter the country is by air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LP1_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-LP1-304">[302]</a></sup> According to the website <i><a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a></i>, getting into Myanmar is problematic: "No bus or train service connects Myanmar with another country, nor can you travel by car or motorcycle across the borderÂ â you must walk across." They further state that "It is not possible for foreigners to go to/from Myanmar by sea or river."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LP1_304-1"><a href="#cite_note-LP1-304">[302]</a></sup> There are a few border crossings that allow the passage of private vehicles, such as the border between <a href="/wiki/Ruili" title="Ruili">Ruili</a> (China) to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muse,_Burma" title="Muse, Burma">Mu-se</a>, the border between <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Htee_Kee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Htee Kee (page does not exist)">Htee Kee</a> (Myanmar) and <a href="/wiki/Phu_Nam_Ron" title="Phu Nam Ron">Phu Nam Ron</a> (Thailand)âthe most direct border between <a href="/wiki/Dawei" title="Dawei">Dawei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kanchanaburi" title="Kanchanaburi">Kanchanaburi</a>, and the border between <a href="/wiki/Myawaddy" title="Myawaddy">Myawaddy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mae_Sot" title="Mae Sot">Mae Sot</a>, Thailand. At least one tourist company has successfully run commercial overland routes through these borders since 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[303]</a></sup>
</p><p>Flights are available from most countries, though direct flights are limited to mainly Thai and other <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> airlines. According to <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_Eleven" title="Weekly Eleven">Eleven</a></i> magazine, "In the past, there were only 15 international airlines and increasing numbers of airlines have begun launching direct flights from Japan, Qatar, Taiwan, South Korea, Germany and Singapore."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11.1_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-11.1-306">[304]</a></sup> Expansions were expected in September 2013 but are mainly <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thai</a> and other Asian-based airlines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11.1_306-1"><a href="#cite_note-11.1-306">[304]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Myanmar" title="Demographics of Myanmar">Demographics of Myanmar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtownflatsyangon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Downtownflatsyangon.jpg/220px-Downtownflatsyangon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Downtownflatsyangon.jpg/330px-Downtownflatsyangon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Downtownflatsyangon.jpg/440px-Downtownflatsyangon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtownflatsyangon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A block of apartments in downtown Yangon, facing <a href="/wiki/Bogyoke_Market" title="Bogyoke Market">Bogyoke Market</a>. Much of Yangon's urban population resides in densely populated flats.</div></div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Myanmar_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>
<p>The provisional results of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Myanmar_Census" title="2014 Myanmar Census">2014 Myanmar Census</a> show that the total population is 51,419,420.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[307]</a></sup> This figure includes an estimated 1,206,353 persons in parts of northern <a href="/wiki/Rakhine_State" title="Rakhine State">Rakhine State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kachin_State" title="Kachin State">Kachin State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kayin_State" title="Kayin State">Kayin State</a> who were not counted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spoor_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-spoor-310">[308]</a></sup> People who were out of the country at the time of the census are not included in these figures. There are over 600,000 registered <a href="/wiki/Migrant_worker" title="Migrant worker">migrant workers</a> from Myanmar in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, and millions more work illegally. Burmese citizens account for 80% of all migrant workers in Thailand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[309]</a></sup> The national population density is 76 per square kilometre (200/sqÂ mi), among the lowest in Southeast Asia.
</p><p>Myanmar's fertility rate as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Myanmar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is 2.23, which is slightly above <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">replacement level</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jon_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-jon-312">[310]</a></sup> and is low compared to <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian countries</a> of similar economic standing, such as <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> (3.18) and Laos (4.41).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jon_312-1"><a href="#cite_note-jon-312">[310]</a></sup> There has been a significant decline in fertility in the 2000s, from a rate of 4.7 children per woman in 1983, down to 2.4 in 2001, despite the absence of any national population policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jon_312-2"><a href="#cite_note-jon-312">[310]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[311]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mya_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-mya-314">[312]</a></sup> The fertility rate is much lower in urban areas.
</p><p>The relatively rapid decline in fertility is attributed to several factors, including extreme delays in marriage (almost unparalleled among developing countries in the region), the prevalence of illegal abortions, and the high proportion of single, unmarried women of reproductive age, with 25.9% of women aged 30â34 and 33.1% of men and women aged 25â34 being single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mya_314-1"><a href="#cite_note-mya-314">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mar_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-mar-315">[313]</a></sup>
</p><p>These patterns stem from economic dynamics, including high income inequality, which results in residents of reproductive age opting for delay of marriage and family-building in favour of attempting to find employment and establish some form of wealth;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mya_314-2"><a href="#cite_note-mya-314">[312]</a></sup> the average age of marriage in Myanmar is 27.5 for men, 26.4 for women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mya_314-3"><a href="#cite_note-mya-314">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mar_315-1"><a href="#cite_note-mar-315">[313]</a></sup>
</p>

<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>
<td style="text-align:left;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magway,_Burma" title="Magway, Burma">Magway</a></td>
